Jamison Brereton

21 (462)
Indra (1тАУ8, 10, 12), All Gods (9, 11)
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
12 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The first p─Бda of this hymn introduces one of its major concerns: the relationship between the current poet and the generations of previous poets to whose lineage he belongs and the question of whether Indra will pay the same attention to the current poet as he did to the older ones (see also vss. 4тАУ6, 8, 10). This theme is connected to the common worry about whether Indra himself exists and, if so, whereтАФsubtly articulated in verses 2 and 4, and triumphantly refuted in the last p─Бda of verse 10. The themes are connected by the anxiety about IndraтАЩs epiphany (see esp. vs. 4). Since the goal of the soma sacrifice is to produce IndraтАЩs epiphany, that is, his appearance at our ritual ground, then his absence may result either from

his favoring another group of sacrificers and poets or from the fact that he doesnтАЩt exist at all!

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese earnest adorations of the much-desiring worshipper glorify you, hero, Indra, who are adorable; mounted on your car, undecaying, ever new, and to whom the wealth (of sacrifice), the most excellent opulence, proceeds.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These insights of this latest of many bards, (insights) deserving to invoke, newly invoke
you who deserve invoking, o hero, the unaging chariot-mounter.
Extensive wealth is sped by their eloquence.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As with hemistich initial #┼Ыata├нс╕е тАж #vadha├нс╕е in VI.20.4 in the immediately preceding hymn, I take #im─Б╠Бс╕е тАж #dh├нyaс╕е as a тАЬverticalтАЭ NP, тАЬthese insights.тАЭ Their positioning allows them to get out of the way of the intense etym. figure in b: h├бvyam тАж h├бvy─Б havante. This figure is complicated by the fact that h├бvya- is used in two slightly different senses, controlled by slightly different constructions of the verb тИЪh┼л / hv─Б. Although the normal object of this verb is a god or other being called upon, very occasionally it can take the call itself as object (see comm. ad IV.23.3), and of course derivatives like h├бva(na)- express the call itself. In our passage havante тАШthey invokeтАЩ takes the usual type of object, namely Indra here, who is qualified by the gerundive h├бvya- тАШto be invokedтАЩ. But the insights (dh├нyaс╕е) themselves are also so qualified; here h├бvy─Бс╕е must mean not тАШto be invokedтАЩ, but тАШto be called [=spoken]тАЩ. In order to keep the vocabulary constant, I have tr. тАШdeserving to invokeтАЩ, in contrast to тАШdeserving to be invokedтАЩ applied to Indra.

The vertical NP just discussed unbalances syntactic constituency, and, unusually, the hemistich boundary cannot be respected.

In d most take ─лyate to тИЪy─Б / ─л тАШimplore, begтАЩ; so, e.g., Geldner тАЬтАж wird тАж erbetenтАЭ (likewise Lubotsky, Kulikov, -ya-presents 495). I assign it rather to тАШspeedsтАЩ, though either is possible.

Griffith

THESE the most constant singer’s invocations call thee who art to be invoked, O Hero;
Hymns call anew the chariot-borne, Eternal: by eloquence men gain abundant riches.

Geldner

Diese einladenden Gebete des ersten Dichters unter den vielen rufen dich, o Held, den zu Ladenden, den Wagenfahrer, den Alterlosen aufs neue. Reichlicher Besitz wird mit Beredsamkeit erbeten.

Grassmann

Den rufenswerthen rufen diese Rufe des emsigsten der Dichter dich, o Starker, Gebete neu den alten Wagenk├дmpfer, durch Liederfleiss wird Gut und Macht erworben.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI glorifyi that Indra who is propitiated by praises, exalted by sacrifices, who knows all things; the magnitude of whom, the possessor of various wisdom, exceeds in vastness (that of) heaven and earth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I will praise him who is known as тАЬIndra,тАЭ whose vehicle is songs, who is strengthened by sacrifice along with songs,
him of many wiles, whose greatness projects beyond heaven and earth in their greatness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The nominal rel. cl. y├│ v├нd─Бnaс╕е, interrupting a string of accusatives, is syntactically curious. It seems to represent a sort of izafe, rather than a real embedded relative cl. I have tr. it as if acc. ├нndram were the predicate of the participle (тАЬwho is known as тАЬIndraтАЭ), despite the difference in cases. Geldner, in contrast: тАЬder bekannt ist.тАЭ My interpr. might be better represented as тАЬI will praise him тАФ Indra, as he is known тАФ whose тАжтАЭ This interpr. fits well with the doubts expressed about Indra later in the hymn, esp. vs. 4. See also v├нd─Бnaс╕е in 12b.

The instr. g─лrbh├нс╕е in b might be better construed with the verb stuс╣гe in a: тАЬI will praise him with songsтАЭ; it has been displaced to the right to be nearer to g├нrv─Бhasam.

The second hemistich contains a strikingly mixed construction, with the usual matched pair heaven and earth in two different cases, acc. d├нvam, abl.-gen. pс╣Ыthivy─Б╠Бс╕е, though construed with the same verb. The two different cases are controlled by two different PREVERB + тИЪric combinations, one overt, one implied. Overt is ├бti тИЪric тАШextend beyond, surpassтАЩ, which is rather rare but takes the acc., as in VIII.92.14, 22 n├б tv─Б╠Бm indr─Б╠Бti ricyate тАЬnothing surpasses you, IndraтАЭ (cf. also X.90.5); hence our тАж d├нvam ├бti тАж riric├й. The implied construction is the more common pr├б тИЪric тАШextend beyondтАЩ which takes the abl., as in I.61.9 asy├йd ev├б pr├б ririce mahitv├бс╣Г, div├бs pс╣Ыthivy─Б╠Бс╕е p├бri ant├бrikс╣г─Бt тАЬhis greatness projected beyond heaven and earth, beyond the midspaceтАЭ (note clear abl. ant├бrikс╣г─Бt) (cf. also I.59.5, 109.6, etc.), hence our тАж pс╣Ыthivy─Б╠Бс╕е тАж ririce mahitv├бm. Examples of this latter constr. are found in this group of Indra hymns (VI.24.3, 30.1), and despite the absence of pr├б here it is not surprising that the abl. construction would creep in.

Griffith

I praise that Indra, known to all men, honoured with songs, extolled with hymns at sacrifices,
Whose majesty, rich in wondrous arts, surpasseth the magnitude of earth, and heaven in greatness.

Geldner

Den Indra will ich mit Lobliedern preisen, der bekannt ist, den die Lobreden anziehen, die Opfer st├дrken, dessen Gr├╢├Яe an Umfang ├╝ber Himmel und Erde hinausreicht, des Verwandlungsreichen.

Grassmann

Den Indra preis ich, der sich finden l├дsset, mit Liedern ihn, der Lieder liebt und Opfer, Den zauberreichen, dessen Gr├╢sse weithin den Himmel und die Erde ├╝berraget.

Elizarenkova

рд╕ рдЗрддреН рд╕ рдПрд╡реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЕрд╡рдпреБрдирдореН рдЕрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН ред рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдирд╛рд╢рдирдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрддрдиреНрд╡рддреН рд╡реГрддреНрд░реЗрдг рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрдВ рддрдордГ рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рдВ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЗрдг рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд░реЛрдкрд┐рддреЗрди рджреЗрд╡реЗрди рд╡рдпреБрдирд╡рддреН рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╡рддреН рдЪрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреГрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рдкрд░реЛрд╜рд░реНрдзрд░реНрдЪрдГ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдХреГрддрдГ ред рд╣реЗ рд╕реНрд╡рдзрд╛рд╡рдГ рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреНрдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░ рдорд░реНрддрд╛рдГ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЕрдореГрддрд╕реНрдп рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рджреАрдпрдВ рдзрд╛рдо рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдЦреНрдпрдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдореН ред рддрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреН рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЗрдпрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрдГ рдпрд╖реНрдЯреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ рдХрджрд╛ рдХрджрд╛рдЪрд┐рддреН ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рди рдорд┐рдирдиреНрддрд┐ рдХрд┐рдордкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдЬрд╛рддрдВ рди рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who made the indistinct, wide-spreading darkness distinct with the sun; whenever, possessor of strength, mortals are seeking to adore the dwelling of you who are an immortal, they harm not (any living being).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Na minanti na hiс╣Гsanti = the object is: kim api praс╣Зij─Бtam

Jamison Brereton

Just he made the patternless darkness in its extension to be patterned by the sun.
When do mortals, seeking gain, not violate the ordinances that belong to you, the immortal, o autonomous one?

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the meaning of vay├║na-, see comm. ad II.34.4.

As has long been known, the RVic desid. stem ├нyakс╣гa- belongs to тИЪna┼Ы тАШattainтАЩ, not (pace Grassmann) тИЪyaj тАШsacrificeтАЩ. See, inter alia, EWA s.v. NA┼Ъ 1 ; Heenen (Desid. 79-82).

The question in the 2nd hemistich seems like a non sequitur, which makes me somewhat sympathetic to S─Бyaс╣ЗaтАЩs reading as a (negative) indefinite: kad─Б cid тАЬthey do not ever violate тАжтАЭ But this reinterpr. is arbitrary, of course, and further, the kad─Б╠Б question inaugurates a series of questions in vs. 4, each with a ka- form: a k├║ha, b k├бm тАж k─Б╠Бsu, c k├бс╕е, d k├бс╕е тАж katam├бс╕е. It may be that we have to ask about the whereabouts of Indra in vs. 4 because he has ceased to appear to us because we have (or may have) violated his ordinances.

Griffith

He hath made pathways, with the Sun to aid him, throughout the darkness that extended pathless.
Mortals who yearn to worship ne’er dishonour, O Mighty God, thy Law who art Immortal.

Geldner

Er hat die ausgebreitete zeitlose Finsternis durch die Sonne zeitlich geregelt. Wann ├╝bertreten die Sterblichen, die ein Begehren haben, nicht deine, des Unsterblichen, Abmachungen, du Selbstherrlicher?

Grassmann

Die Finsterniss, die weit sich dehnte, lichtlos, die machte er hellleuchtend durch die Sonne; Niemals verletzen Menschen eifrig opfernd des Ewigen Gesetz, o Machtbegabter.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhat is he, the Indra who has done these deeds? What region does he frequent? Amog what people (does he abide)? What worship, Indra, gives satisfaction to your mind? What praise is able to gratify you? Which of your invokers (is most acceptable to you)?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He who did these things, where then is heтАФthis тАЬIndraтАЭ? Upon what people does he attend? Among which clans?
What sacrifice is weal for your thought, your wish? What chant, Indra? Which one is your Hotar?

Jamison Brereton Notes

-tama-forms implicitly index a referent among three or more possibilities.

The interrog. katam├б- here echoes purut├бma- of 1a. I have chosen to render katam├бwith the heavy tr. тАШwhich of manyтАЩ because in this series of questions the poet is anxiously surveying all the possible sacrifices and sacrificers who may have attracted Indra away from us.

Griffith

And he who did these things, where is that Indra? among what tribes? what people doth he visit?
What sacrifice contents thy mind , and wishes? What priest among them all? what hymn, O Indra?

Geldner

Wo ist denn der Indra, der das getan hat; zu welchem Volke geht er, bei welchen St├дmmen ist er? Welches Opfer ist deinem Sinne recht nach Wunsch, welches Loblied, o Indra, welcher ist der Opferpriester?

Grassmann

Wo ist doch Indra, welcher dies vollbrachte? zu welchem Manne geht er? welchen H├дusern? Welch Opfer mundet deinem Sinn und Wunsche? welch Lied, o Indra? welches ist der Priester?

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDoer of many deeds, these adders, born in former times, engaged in sacred rites, have been, as they are now, your friends; so have those of mediaeval and those of recent (date); therefore, invoked of many, take notice of your (present) humble (adorer).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For up to now they have been ever toiling for you, o doer of many (deeds)тАФthose who were born long ago, your ancient comrades,
those in between, and the current ones. Much-invoked one, take
cognizance of the one who is closest.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ut├б in the middle of p─Бda c uncomplicatedly conjoins the temporally contrastive madhyam─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАЬthe middle ones, those in betweenтАЭ and n┼л╠Бtan─Бsaс╕е тАЬthe current onesтАЭ (see Klein DGRV I.301, 311), but the one beginning p─Бda d, in KleinтАЩs words (DGRV I.382) тАЬintroduc[es] a new nonparallel clause.тАЭ It is not represented in the published translation, which should perhaps read тАЬAnd тАж take cognizance of the one who is closest.тАЭ The reason for this apparently pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ conjunction may be that тАЬthe closest oneтАЭ (singular avam├б-) is not only a subset of тАЬthe current onesтАЭ (plural n┼л╠Бtan─Бsaс╕е), but the climax of the series of temporally sorted comrades.

Griffith

Yea, here were they who, born of old, have served thee, thy friends of ancient time, thou active Worker.
Bethink thee now of these, Invoked of many! the midmost and the recent, and the youngest.

Geldner

Denn zu dieser Stunde pflegten die fr├╝hgeborenen vormaligen Genossen f├╝r dich des Dienstes zu walten, du Vielwirkender, und tun es die mittleren und neueren. Achte auch des J├╝ngsten, du Vielgerufener!

Grassmann

Hier waren dir, dem emsigen, ja alte und urgeborne Freunde, thatenreicher, Sei achtsam auf die mittleren und neuen und auf den j├╝ngsten auch, o vielgerufner.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHumble (worshippers), adoring him, commemorate, Indra, your excellent, ancient, and glorious (deeds); so, hero, who are attracted by prayer, we praise you who are mighty, for those great actions with which we are acquained.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who are attracted by prayer: brahmav─Бhaс╕е = mantrairvahan─лya, to be borne or conveyed by prayers

Jamison Brereton

The closer ones, asking about him, have guided themselves following your distant, ancient (acts) worthy of fame, Indra.
As far as we know it, that far we chant to you as the great one, you hero with the sacred formulation as your vehicle.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This ultimate insider, тАЬthe closest oneтАЭ of 5d, is immediately picked up by the slightly more distanced тАЬcloser onesтАЭ (├бvar─Бsaс╕е) in 6a. Here their comparative closeness is not contrasted with previous generations of IndraтАЩs comrades, as in vs. 5, but with the older, distant deeds of Indra. These closer one are тАЬaskingтАЭ (pс╣Ыch├бntaс╕е) about Indra. Their asking may refer directly to the questions in vs. 4, but it also implies that, however тАЬcloseтАЭ they are, they do not have direct access to knowledge about Indra.

The limits on our knowledge are explicitly acknowledged in the 2nd hemistich, where we praise Indra only insofar as know him (y─Б╠Бd ev├б vidm├б). This subordinated expression is embedded in the larger clause: ├бrc─Бmasi тАж, y─Б╠Бd ev├б vidm├б t─Б╠Бt tv─Б mah─Б╠Бntam, where the obj. of ├бrc─Бmasi is tv─Б, but the y─Б╠Бd тАж t─Б╠Бd diptych is clearly formulaic and frozen. This expression reminds us slightly of the y├│ v├нd─Бnaс╕е of 2b, likewise with тИЪvid тАШknowтАЩ and likewise technically embedded.

Griffith

Inquiring after him, thy later servants, Indra, have gained thy former old traditions.
Hero, to whom the prayer is brought, we praise thee as great for that wherein we know thee mighty.

Geldner

Ihn danach fragend halten sich die J├╝ngeren an deine l├дngst vergangenen ehemaligen Ruhmestaten, o Indra. Wir preisen dich, du Held, den das Segenswort anzieht, als den Gro├Яen, soweit als wir es verstehen.

Grassmann

Die j├╝ngern, fragend nach den fr├╝hern Thaten, o Indra, strebten nach den altber├╝hmten; Wir preisen dich, o Held, Gebetempf├дnger, so weit wir es verstehen, dich, den grossen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe strength of the r─Бkс╣гasas is concentrated against you; bear up well against that mighty manifested (effort); scatter them, valiant (Indra), with your old associate, your friend, the thunderbolt.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The face of the demon has spread out against you, who were born great. Stand up to it well!
With your ancient, conjoined comrade, your mace, o bold one, thrust these away.

Jamison Brereton Notes

JPB suggests that the тАЬface of the demonтАЭ spreading out against Indra is hood of the cobra, namely Vс╣Ыtra.

The referent of the expression beginning b, m├бhi jaj├▒─Бn├бm тАЬhaving been born great,тАЭ is entirely ambiguous. It may be, as the published translation takes it, an acc. with tv─Б, referring to Indra. Or it may be, as Grassmann and Geldner take it, a neut. nom. modifying the neut.

s-stem p─Б╠Бjaс╕е. Technically speaking, of course, m├бhi is neut. and might therefore give weight to the latter possibility. But m├бhi can be adverbial here, evoking the apparently fixed expression m├бhi j─Бt├бm (I.163.1, III.31.3, cf. I.156.2); cf. also V.60.3 m├бhi vс╣Ыddh├бс╕е тАШgrown greatтАЩ. I now think the ambigity is meant, and the phrase can apply to either of the antagonists (or rather, in the case of the rakс╣г├бs-) its visage. The ambiguity is hard to convey in tr.; perhaps тАЬтАж (each) born great.тАЭ The two verbs in the first hemistich, abh├н тАж v├н tasthe# and тАж abh├н тАж tiс╣гс╣нha#, belong to the same root (тИЪsth─Б), are positioned identically, and differ fairly minimally from each other: tense-aspect stem, voice, person, as well as an extra preverb with the first. Unfortunately the etymological connection canтАЩt be easily capture in tr.: тАЬhas stood wide against youтАЭ is unidiomatic and opaque.

The 2nd hemistich seems implicitly to convey that our anxieties about our intimacy with Indra were well-founded. In 5ab our forebears were identified as IndraтАЩs тАЬancient comradesтАЭ (pratn─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАж s├бkh─Бyaс╕е), with later generations apparently grandfathered into this select group (5cd). But here we learn who IndraтАЩs тАЬancient comradeтАЭ really is тАФ his mace: t├бva pratn├йna y├║jyena s├бkhy─Б v├бjreс╣Зa.

Griffith

The demon’s strength is gathered fast against thee: great as that strength hath grown, go forth to meet it.
With thine own ancient friend and companion, the thunderbolt, brave Champion! drive it backward.

Geldner

English translation:

тАЬSupporter of (your) worshippers, hero, Indra, listen (to the praises) of your present adorer, for you have always attended to invocations at sacrifices in ancient times, as the kinsman of our forefather.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Pitс╣Ыс╣З─Бm ─Бpiс╕е = bandhuс╕е; aс╣Еgirasas are intended

Jamison Brereton

Listen, Indra, to the current (bard) creating sacred formulations, you hero who give succor to bardsтАФ
for you, as the friend of our ancestors in olden days, have always been easy to invoke in the quest.

Griffith

Hear, too, the prayer of this thy present beadsman, O Indra, Hero, cherishing the singer.
For thou wast aye our fathers’ Friend aforetime, still swift to listen to their supplication.

English translation:

тАЬPropitiate today, for our protection and preservation, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Indra and the Maruts, P┼лс╣гan, Viс╣гс╣Зu, Agni, of many rites, Savit─Б, the herbs, the mountains.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bring forward for help Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Indra, and the Maruts, to help us today,
forward P┼лс╣гan, Viс╣гс╣Зu, Agni and Plenty, Savitar, the plants, and the
mountains.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The use of parallel and etymologically related purpose datives ┼лt├бye and ├бvase, stationed in the a and b p─Бdas respectively, seems pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++. I have tr. one as nominal and one as infinitival, but this distinction rests on nothing in the passage.

Griffith

Bring to our help this day, for our protection, Varuna, Mitra , Indra, and the Maruts,
Pusan and Visnu, Agni and Purandhi, Savitar also, and the Plants and Mountains.

Geldner

Mache den Varuna, Mitra, Indra, die Marut heute uns zur Gnade geneigt, mache den Pusan, Vishnu, Agni, Purandhi, Savitri, die Pflanzen und Berge geneigt!

Grassmann

Schaff her zur Huld uns Varuna und Mitra, die Marutschar, den Indra heut zur H├╝lfe, Den Puschan, Vischnu, Agni und Purandhi, den Savitar, die Pflanzen und die Berge.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, of great power, and to be devoutly worshipped, these your adorers glorify you with hymns; do you, who are invoked, hear the invocation of (him) invoking you, for there is no other divinity than you, immortal (Indra), such as you are.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These singers here with their chants chant to you, o you of many talents, receiving the first of the sacrifice.
Listen to the call of him who calls you here as you are called. Immortal one, there exists no one like you, other than you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Like 1b, p─Бda c here contains an extravagant etymological figure based again on тИЪhv─Б тАШcallтАЩ: h├бvam (─Б╠Б) huvat├│ huv─Бn├бс╕е.

The phrasing of d also seems awkwardly pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ – n├б tv─Б╠Бv─Бm╠Рany├бс╕е .. tv├бd asti тАЬno one like you exists, other than youтАЭ – in comparison with the usual expression, found in nearby VI.30.4 n├б tv─Б╠Бv─Бm╠Рany├│ asti тАЬthere exists no one else like youтАЭ (cf. VII.32.23).

Griffith

The singers here exalt with hymns and praises thee who art very Mighty and Most Holy.
Hear, when invoked, the invoker’s invocation. Beside thee there is nonelike thee, Immortal!

Geldner

Diese S├дnger besingen dich, du Vielverm├╢gender, Opfersamer, mit Preisliedern. Gerufen erh├╢re den Ruf des Rufenden. Nicht gibt es au├Яer dir einen anderen, der dir gleicht, du Unsterblicher.

Grassmann

Es preisen, hochverehrter, kraftbegabter, hier diese S├дnger dich mit Preisges├дngen; Vernimm den Ruf des rufenden, gerufner, kein andrer ist, unsterblicher, wie du bist.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome quickly, son of strength, you who know (all things), upon my prayer; together with all the adorable (divinities); they who, with the tongue of Agni, are partakers of the sacrifice, who rendered Manu (victorious) over his adversaries.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ye manum cakrur uparam dus─Бya ┼Ыatr┼лс╣З─Бm or dasy┼лn─Бm uparibhavam = who made Manu the r─Бjarс╣гi, manum r─Бjarс╣гim, over or the overcomer of enemies, or the Dasyus

Jamison Brereton

Now drive here, right up to my speech, since you know, o son of strength, together with all those worthy of the sacrifice,
who had Agni as their tongue and served the truth, who put Manu very close to Dasa.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In c Geldner tr. ─Бs├║с╕е as if it were a present: тАЬdie Agni zur Zunge haben und die Wahrheit pflegen.тАЭ Although this is contextually tempting, the pf. of тИЪas is never presential. Cf. K├╝mmel (111): тАЬEs ist stets (zumindest auch) vergangenheits bezogen gebraucht.тАЭ At best we could render it тАЬwho have (always) had Agni as their tongue тАжтАЭ; this might in fact be better.

In any case the pf. ─Бs├║с╕е in c matches cakr├║с╕е in d, and this latter action appears to be one in the distant past – even though itтАЩs not entirely clear what action it refers to. Interpr. is not helped by the fact that d├бsa- is a hapax, though it is reasonable, with Geldner (n. 11d), to take it as тАЬder mythische Stammvater der D─БsaтАЩs oder DasyuтАЩs,тАЭ or indeed referentially identical with the well-attested stem d─Б╠Бsa- referring to some variety of enemy to the ─Аrya (see Oldenberg, etc.). But what the relationship between Manu and Dasa is in this passage and what the gods were attempting to bring about are both unclear – an unclarity also facilitated by the ambiguity of ├║para-, which can mean, inter alia, тАШlowerтАЩ, тАШcloserтАЩ, or тАШlaterтАЩ. The published translation тАЬтАж put Manu very close to DasaтАЭ is opaque; in fact I do not now know what I meant by it. Geldner takes ├║para- as тАШlaterтАЩ and assumes that the gods made Manu DasaтАЩs successor (Nachfolger). I am now inclined towards OldenbergтАЩs solution, however: that the gods put Manu below (the тАШlowerтАЩ sense of ├║para-) in the earthly region тАЬfor Dasa,тАЭ with the dative of malefit, not benefit: they set Manu to do to Dasa whatever he deserved. Michael Weiss comments тАЬWouldn’t this most sense if it meant ’they made Manus superior to DasaтАЩ? Could the original meaning of *upara- as preserved in Avestan, be kept here? For the sentiment cf. VI.19.13 ┼Ы├бtroс╕е-┼Ыatror ├║ttara ├нt sy─Бma.тАЭ this would be a neat solution, though I wonder whether a reading that requires the opposite sense (тАШaboveтАЩ) of one of the senses of this stem (тАШlowerтАЩ) would be available.

Griffith

Now to my words come quickly thou who knowest, O Son of Strength, with all who claim our worship,
Who visit sacred rites, whose tongue is Agni, Gods who made Manu stronger than the Dasyu.

Geldner

Nun komme her, auf meine Rede, sie verstehend, du Sohn der St├дrke, die den Manu dem Dasa zum Nachfolger gemacht haben!

Grassmann

Nun komme kundig her zu meinem Liede, o Sohn der Kraft mit allen opferwerthen, Die stets aus Agni tranken, Opfer hegten, den Menschen setzten ├╝ber die D├дmonen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬConstructor of paths, who are cognizant (of all things), be our preceder, whether in easy or difficult (ways); bring to us food, Indra, with those your (steeds), who are unwearied, large, and bearers of great burdens.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Become a leader for us on easy roads and on difficult ones, since you are known as a path-maker.
The broad, unflagging (horses), the best conveyorsтАФwith them convey the prize to us, o Indra.

On good and evil ways be thou our Leader, thou who art known to all as Path-preparer.
Bring power to us, O Indra, with thy Horses, Steeds that are best to draw, broad-backed, unwearied.

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рдордВрдЧрд▓ рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд░рд╛, рд╕реНрд╡рддрдГ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдд рдЪрд╛рд▓рдгрд╛рд░рд╛ рд╡ рдЗрддрд░рд╛рдВрдирд╛рд╣реА рдЪрд╛рд▓рд╡рд┐рдгрд╛рд░рд╛, рдЕрд╕рддреЛ рддреЛрдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рди рдЕрд╕рддреЛ. рдЬреЛ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╕рддреНрд╕рдВрдЧ рдХрд░рддреЛ рддреЛрдЪ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдд рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╣реЛрдКрди рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рджреЗрдгреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЕрд╕рддреЛ. рее резреи рее
